I had one shirt that was basically all scuffed up on the back from a zipline harness. I don&#x27;t have a picture before using this fabric shaver but here&#x27;s took a picture of what it looks like afterwards. This t-shirt is 60% cotton and 40% polyester like most of my shirts. I did the best I could with removing the fuzzballs and in the end, the shirt&#x27;s fabric look a little washed out. There were still some fuzziness but the shaver couldn&#x27;t remove those anymore. This shaver does a good job in most cases when it&#x27;s a small job. In my extreme case, the harness I was wearing for my zipline adventure just caused way too much damage. Other shirts that have less fuzzballs are removed without any issues.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;We have since used this shaver on other fabrics like bed sheets, pillow cases and blankets. Unless those bed fabrics are torn or very old, there should no need to throw them away. If you look at the two pictures of the before and after on the bedsheet, you will notice a huge difference. It&#x27;s just a corner of the bedsheet and it took just a few minutes to remove basically most of the fuzzballs.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;One thing to note is that it will not pick up any hair or loose particles unless it&#x27;s stuck to the fabric and is small/rounded enough to fit into the shaving head area. I actually have a small tear on the sheet and rolled over it with the shaver to see if it will snip it off. It just went by it without the blades cutting it. This is probably for the best since the purpose of this shaver it to remove fuzzballs.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;After you&#x27;re done using the fabric shaver, I recommend just emptying the small container with all the shaved fabric. It&#x27;s usually a simple cleaning but if it&#x27;s a long or big job, there tends to be some additional fabric stuck where the blade is. I usually use a small set of tweezers and slowly pull them out from the bottom. You can also remove the face plate and try removing it there but I find it more effective removing from the bottom of the device.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The shaver is pretty lightweight and operates on two AA batteries which are not included.     <li> I wanted to like this because the fuzzbuster of my youth was a Remington, and it was great and lasted forever. And while this is a very effective fuzzbuster (blew my drugstore one out of the water), it has some major flaws that have sent me looking for a replacement, namely:  - The holes in the cap are too big, making this a danger to delicate (and even not-so-delicate) fabrics. I made the mistake of fuzzbusting a delicately knit sweater and it chopped several holes in it (and I am very careful!). I also did a terrycloth jacket, and while it didn&#x27;t chop holes, it DID nick it in several places, pulling threads out of place.  - The supposedly ergonomic design is not so ergonomic. When cleaning fabric, I always hold the fabric in my left hand, with my hand beneath the area I&#x27;m cleaning, and then use my right hand to do the fuzzbusting. The only way this Remington would be ergonomic is if you held it in your hand at the angle shown in the picture. But to actually be effective, you need to hold it 90 degrees down from what the picture shows, meaning either the pointed end is in the palm of your hand or your wrist is awkwardly at 90 degrees. Not very comfortable.  - My final complaint is the fuzz holder. It seems to have a smaller capacity than other small fuzzbusters I&#x27;ve used, and because of the so-called ergonomic design of the whole device, the hole from the blade area into the receptacle is small and narrow. So the fuzz ends up getting stuck in the blade area, and you have to remove the cap, remove the blades, and clear it out. Also, the fuzz that does manage to get into the container gets stuck in the plastic seam, which isn&#x27;t sealed, but also isn&#x27;t removable. What a pain!  In short, I wouldn&#x27;t recommend buying this. Find a traditionally-shaped fuzzbuster with smaller holes in the cap...that&#x27;s what I&#x27;m looking for.</li>

It&#x27;s bound to happen every so often, and you can use the shaver to go over the spot and take down any new loose threads you&#x27;ve created, but if you aren&#x27;t careful this will happen a lot and you will probably end up ruining your shirt.     <li> This device is meant for shaving off all those little fuzz balls that build up on some materials and can make a sweater, for example, look too well-worn.  I remember when these devices were first introduced, and the manufacturers were so afraid of clothing damage that the holes were too small and then the product didn&#x27;t even work (big fabric &#x27;pills&#x27; could not fit into the holes to be snipped off!). Now some reviewers complain of fabric damage because now the holes are too big.  So...what size hole in front of the blade is &#x27;just right&#x27;?  (sound like a Goldilocks story? :-) I think the size of the holes in this shaver are just right!  Be aware that these type shavers are really designed for heavier type fabrics (think of sweaters, comforters, socks...) that tend to pill up easily (especially wools &amp; fuzzy acrylics) and fabrics that are NOT very fragile, vs sheers and silks.  So just be cautious if you choose to use it on more delicate fabrics.  On delicate fabrics, I&#x27;d recommend the obvious: try an inconspicuous area first, and stretch the fabric very firmly while you shave it so it can&#x27;t be pulled inside the device.  Using this method (which really should be used no matter WHAT type of fabric!) I&#x27;ve shaved heavy fabrics and sheer fabrics, and not had any problems!  I recommend!  (I would have given this 5 stars if it was priced slightly lower)</li>
